Automatically classifies tasks into compliance tiers and enforces appropriate verification.\n\n**Key Benefits**:\n- Single command replaces confusion between `sc:task` and `sc:task-mcp`\n- Automatic tier classification with confidence scoring\n- Appropriate verification for each task type\n- Prevents over-engineering for trivial changes\n- Ensures safety for critical changes\n\n## Triggers\n\nUse `/sc:task` when:\n- Task involves code modifications with downstream impacts\n- Complexity score >0.6 with code modifications\n- Multi-file scope (>2 estimated affected files)\n- Security domain paths detected (auth/, security/, crypto/)\n- Refactoring or system-wide changes requested\n\n**Auto-Suggest Keywords**:\n- High confidence: \"implement feature\", \"refactor system\", \"fix security\", \"add authentication\", \"update database schema\"\n- Moderate confidence: \"add new\", \"create component\", \"update service\", \"modify API\"\n\n## Usage\n\n```bash\n/sc:task [description]                           # Auto-detect all dimensions\n/sc:task [description] --compliance strict       # Force STRICT tier\n/sc:task [description] --compliance light        # Force LIGHT tier\n/sc:task [description] --skip-compliance         # Bypass compliance (escape hatch)\n/sc:task [description] --verify auto             # Auto-select verification\n```\n\n## Behavioral Flow\n\n### 0. Classification (Already Performed)\n\nClassification was handled by the `/sc:task` command before this skill was invoked. The tier has been determined and the classification header has been emitted. Proceed directly to execution based on the classified tier.\n\n**Reference** — the tier keyword tables (for context only, do not re-classify):\n- **STRICT**: security, authentication, database, migration, refactor, breaking change, encrypt, token, session, oauth\n- **EXEMPT**: explain, search, commit, push, plan, discuss, brainstorm\n- **LIGHT**: typo, comment, whitespace, lint, docstring, formatting, minor\n- **STANDARD**: implement, add, create, update, fix, build, modify, change (default)\n\n### 2. Confidence Display (Human-Readable)\n\nAfter the mandatory classification header, show a human-readable summary:\n\n```\n**Tier: STANDARD** [████████░░] 80%\n\nClassified as STANDARD:\n- Keywords matched: add, implement\n- Confidence score: 0.78\n- Considered alternatives: STRICT (0.35)\n```\n\nIf confidence <70%, add prompt: \"⚠️ Low confidence. Override with: `--compliance [strict|standard|light|exempt]`\"\n\n**Note**: The machine-readable header (Section 0) is for telemetry/A/B testing. This human-readable display is for user understanding.\n\n### 3. Execution Phase\n\nExecute task according to tier requirements:\n\n**STRICT Execution**:\n1. Activate project (mcp__serena__activate_project)\n2. Verify git working directory clean (git status)\n3. Load codebase context (codebase-retrieval)\n4. Check relevant memories (list_memories -> read_memory)\n5. Identify all affected files and test files\n6. Make changes with full checklist\n7. Identify all files that import changed code\n8. Update all affected files\n9. Spawn verification agent (quality-engineer)\n10. Run comprehensive tests: `pytest [path] -v`\n11. Answer adversarial questions\n\n**STANDARD Execution**:\n1. Load context via codebase-retrieval\n2. Search downstream impacts (find_referencing_symbols OR grep)\n3. Make changes\n4. Run affected tests OR document manual verification\n5. Verify basic functionality\n\n**LIGHT Execution**:\n1. Quick scope check (files/lines within bounds)\n2. Make changes\n3. Quick sanity check (syntax valid, no obvious errors)\n4. Proceed with judgment\n\n**EXEMPT Execution**:\n1. Execute immediately\n2. No verification overhead\n\n### 4. Verification Phase\n\nRoute to appropriate verification based on tier and paths:\n\n| Compliance Tier | Verification Method | Token Cost | Timeout |\n|-----------------|---------------------|------------|---------|\n| STRICT | Sub-agent (quality-engineer) | 3-5K | 60s |\n| STANDARD | Direct test execution | 300-500 | 30s |\n| LIGHT | Skip verification | 0 | 0s |\n| EXEMPT | Skip verification | 0 | 0s |\n\n**Critical Path Override**: Paths matching `auth/`, `security/`, `crypto/`, `models/`, `migrations/` always trigger CRITICAL verification regardless of compliance tier.\n\n**Trivial Path Override**: Paths matching `*.md`, `docs/`, `*test*.py` may skip verification.\n\n### 5. Feedback Collection\n\nAfter completion, collect implicit feedback:\n- Track if user overrode tier (implicit classification feedback)\n- Note smooth completion vs errors (quality signal)\n- Store for calibration learning\n\n## MCP Integration\n\n**Required Servers by Tier**:\n- STRICT: Sequential, Serena (fallback not allowed)\n- STANDARD: Sequential, Context7 (fallback allowed)\n- LIGHT: None required (fallback allowed)\n- EXEMPT: None required\n\n**Circuit Breaker Behavior**:\n- If required servers unavailable for STRICT tier, block task execution\n- For other tiers, use fallbacks with noted limitations\n\n## Tool Coordination\n\n**Planning Phase**:\n1. TodoWrite: Create task breakdown\n2. codebase-retrieval: Load context\n3. list_memories / read_memory: Check project state\n\n**Execution Phase**:\n1. Edit/MultiEdit/Write: Make changes\n2. Grep/Glob: Find references\n3. find_referencing_symbols: Trace dependencies\n\n**Verification Phase**:\n1. Task (quality-engineer): Spawn verification agent (STRICT only)\n2. Bash: Run tests directly (STANDARD)\n3. think_about_task_adherence: Reflect on completeness\n\n**Completion Phase**:\n1. write_memory: Save session state\n2. think_about_whether_you_are_done: Final check\n\n## Examples\n\n### STRICT Task\n```\n/sc:task \"implement user authentication with JWT\"\n\n-> Classified as STRICT (security domain, authentication keyword)\n-> Full 6-category checklist enforced\n-> Verification agent spawned\n-> Adversarial questions answered\n```\n\n### STANDARD Task\n```\n/sc:task \"add pagination to user list\"\n\n-> Classified as STANDARD (add keyword, typical feature)\n-> Context loaded before editing\n-> Downstream impacts checked\n-> Direct test execution\n```\n\n### LIGHT Task\n```\n/sc:task \"fix typo in README\"\n\n-> Classified as LIGHT (trivial keyword, documentation path)\n-> Quick sanity check only\n-> No verification delay\n```\n\n### EXEMPT Task\n```\n/sc:task \"explain how the auth flow works\"\n\n-> Classified as EXEMPT (explain pattern detected)\n-> Immediate execution\n-> No compliance overhead\n```\n\n### Override Example\n```\n/sc:task \"update config file\" --compliance strict\n\n-> User override to STRICT regardless of classification\n-> Full verification enforced\n```\n\n## Boundaries\n\n**Will:**\n- Classify tasks into appropriate compliance tiers\n- Enforce tier-appropriate verification requirements\n- Provide confidence scoring with rationale\n- Track feedback for continuous calibration\n- Support user overrides with justification\n\n**Will Not:**\n- Skip safety-critical verification for STRICT tasks\n- Apply STRICT overhead to genuinely trivial changes\n- Override user's explicit compliance choice\n- Proceed with <70% confidence without user confirmation\n\n## Success Criteria\n\n| Metric | Target | Measurement |\n|--------|--------|-------------|\n| Tier classification accuracy | >=80% | User feedback on appropriateness |\n| User confusion rate | <10% | \"Which command?\" questions eliminated {"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01QUYJwmcNFXCbdHUBA5DCCr","type":"tool_result","content":"     1→\"\"\"Pipeline gate validation -- pure Python, no subprocess, no LLM invocation.\n     2→\n     3→Validates step outputs against GateCriteria with tier-proportional checks:\n     4→  EXEMPT  -> always passes\n     5→  LIGHT   -> file exists + non-empty\n     6→  STANDARD -> + min lines + YAML frontmatter fields\n     7→  STRICT  -> + semantic checks (if defined)\n     8→\n     9→NFR-003: No subprocess import. NFR-007: No sprint/roadmap imports.\n    10→\"\"\"\n    11→\n    12→from __future__ import annotations\n    13→\n    14→from pathlib import Path\n    15→\n    16→from .models import GateCriteria, SemanticCheck\n    17→\n    18→\n    19→def gate_passed(output_file: Path, criteria: GateCriteria) -> tuple[bool, str | None]:\n    20→    \"\"\"Validate a step's output against its gate criteria.\n    21→\n    22→    Returns (True, None) on pass.\n    23→    Returns (False, reason) on failure where reason is human-readable.\n    24→    \"\"\"\n    25→    tier = criteria.enforcement_tier\n    26→\n    27→    # EXEMPT: always passes\n    28→    if tier == \"EXEMPT\":\n    29→        return True, None\n    30→\n    31→    # LIGHT, STANDARD, STRICT: file must exist\n    32→    if not output_file.exists():\n    33→        return False, f\"File not found: {output_file}\"\n    34→\n    35→    # LIGHT, STANDARD, STRICT: file must be non-empty\n    36→    content = output_file.read_text(encoding=\"utf-8\")\n    37→    if len(content.strip()) == 0:\n    38→        return False, f\"File empty (0 bytes): {output_file}\"\n    39→\n    40→    # LIGHT stops here\n    41→    if tier == \"LIGHT\":\n    42→        return True, None\n    43→\n    44→    # STANDARD, STRICT: minimum line count\n    45→    lines = content.splitlines()\n    46→    if len(lines) < criteria.min_lines:\n    47→        return False, (\n    48→            f\"Below minimum line count: {len(lines)} < {criteria.min_lines} \"\n    49→            f\"in {output_file}\"\n    50→        )\n    51→\n    52→    # STANDARD, STRICT: YAML frontmatter fields\n    53→    if criteria.required_frontmatter_fields:\n    54→        ok, reason = _check_frontmatter(content, criteria.required_frontmatter_fields, output_file)\n    55→        if not ok:\n    56→            return False, reason\n    57→\n    58→    # STANDARD stops here\n    59→    if tier == \"STANDARD\":\n    60→        return True, None\n    61→\n    62→    # STRICT: semantic checks\n    63→    if criteria.semantic_checks:\n    64→        for check in criteria.semantic_checks:\n    65→            if not check.check_fn(content):\n    66→                return False, f\"Semantic check '{check.name}' failed: {check.failure_message}\"\n    67→\n    68→    return True, None\n    69→\n    70→\n    71→def _check_frontmatter(\n    72→    content: str, required_fields: list[str], output_file: Path\n    73→) -> tuple[bool, str | None]:\n    74→    \"\"\"Extract and validate YAML frontmatter fields.\"\"\"\n    75→    # Returns when all complete or one fails.\n\n    Cross-cancellation: if any step fails after retry, a shared Event\n    is set, causing remaining steps to terminate their subprocesses.\n    \"\"\"\n    cancel_event = threading.Event()\n    results: list[StepResult | None] = [None] * len(steps)\n\n    def _worker(idx: int, step: Step) -> None:\n        def combined_cancel() -> bool:\n            return cancel_check() or cancel_event.is_set()\n\n        result = _execute_single_step(step, config, run_step, combined_cancel)\n        results[idx] = result\n        if result.status != StepStatus.PASS:\n            cancel_event.set()\n\n    threads = [\n        threading.Thread(target=_worker, args=(i, s), daemon=True)\n        for i, s in enumerate(steps)\n    ]\n    for t in threads:\n        t.start()\n    for t in threads:\n        t.join()\n\n    # Replace None entries (shouldn't happen, but defensive)\n    final: list[StepResult] = []\n    for i, r in enumerate(results):\n        if r is not None:\n            final.append(r)\n        else:\n            now = datetime.now(timezone.utc)\n            final.append(StepResult(\n                step=steps[i],\n                status=StepStatus.CANCELLED,\n                attempt=0,\n                gate_failure_reason=\"Thread did not produce a result\",\n                started_at=now,\n                finished_at=now,\n            ))\n\n    return final\n\n\ndef _build_state(results: list[StepResult]) -> dict:\n    \"\"\"Build a state dict from accumulated results.\"\"\"\n    return {\n        \"steps\": {\n            r.step.id: {\n                \"status\": r.status.value,\n                \"attempt\": r.attempt,\n                \"gate_failure_reason\": r.gate_failure_reason,\n            }\n            for r in results\n        },\n        \"total\": len(results),\n        \"passed\": sum(1 for r in results if r.status == StepStatus.PASS),\n        \"failed\": sum(1 for r in results if r.status.is_failure),\n    }\n","numLines":266,"startLine":1,"totalLines":266}}}

re.compile(r\"\\s+(AND|OR)\\s+\", re.IGNORECASE)\n\n# A clause must contain a comparison operator surrounded by non-empty LHS and RHS.\n_CLAUSE_RE = re.compile(\n Below 0.7 = flagged for review.\n    \"\"\"\n    variable_name: str\n    deliverable_id: str\n    introduction_type: IntroductionType\n    confidence: float = 1.0\n\n    @property\n    def needs_review(self) -> bool:\n        return self.confidence < 0.7\n\n\n# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------\n# Detection patterns\n# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------\n\n# self._field patterns\n_SELF_FIELD_RE = re.compile(r\"self\\.(_\\w+)\")\n\n# Explicit introduction patterns\n_INTRO_PATTERNS = [\n    # Low-confidence detections\n    (confidence < 0.7) are flagged for human review.\n\n    Multiple variables from a single deliverable are all returned.\n    Documentation-only deliverables are excluded.\n    \"\"\"\n    results: list[DetectionResult] = []\n\n    for d in deliverables:\n        desc = d.description\n        if not desc or not desc.strip():\n            continue\n\n        # Documentation suppression\n        if _DOC_SUPPRESSION_RE.search(desc) and not _has_strong_state_signal(desc):\n            continue\n\n        found = _detect_from_description(desc, d.id)\n        results.extend(found)\n\n    return results\n\n\ndef _has_strong_state_signal(desc: str) -> bool:\n    \"\"\"Check if description has strong state variable signals despite doc verbs.\"\"\"\n    lower = desc.lower()\n    if _SELF_FIELD_RE.search(lower):\n        return True\n    for keyword in (\"counter\", \"offset\", \"cursor\", \"flag\", \"replace\"):\n        if keyword in lower:\n            return True\n    return False\n\n\ndef _detect_from_description(desc: str, deliverable_id: str) -> list[DetectionResult]:\n    \"\"\"Extract state variable detections from a single description.\"\"\"\n    results: list[DetectionResult] = []\n    seen_vars: set[str] = set()\n\n    # 1. self._field patterns (highest confidence)\n    for match in _SELF_FIELD_RE.finditer(desc):\n        var_name = match.group(1)\n        if var_name not in seen_vars:\n            seen_vars.add(var_name)\n            results.append(DetectionResult(\n                variable_name=var_name,\n                deliverable_id=deliverable_id,\n                introduction_type=IntroductionType.SELF_ASSIGNMENT,\n                confidence=0.95,\n            ))\n\n    # 2.   -> \"4\"\n    \"\"\"\n    # Try D{number}.{seq} format first\n    m = re.match(r\"D(\\d+)\\.\", deliverable_id)\n    if m:\n        return m.group(1)\n\n    # Try D-{number} format\n    m = max_checks_per_variable: int = DEFAULT_MAX_INVARIANT_CHECKS,\n) -> list[Deliverable]:\n    \"\"\"Generate invariant_check deliverables from mutation inventory.\n\n    For each mutation site (up to max_checks_per_variable), emits a\n    deliverable with kind=invariant_check containing:\n    - The invariant predicate being verified\n    - The specific mutation expression\n    - Applicable edge cases\n\n    Returns list of generated Deliverable objects.\n    \"\"\"\n    generated: list[Deliverable] = []\n\n    # Build lookup from variable_name -> InvariantEntry\n    entry_lookup: dict[str, InvariantEntry] = {}\n    for entry in invariant_entries:\n        entry_lookup[entry.variable_name] = entry\n\n    for inv_result in inventory_results:\n        entry = entry_lookup.get(inv_result.variable_name)\n        if entry is None:\n            continue\n\n        # Cap at max_checks_per_variable\n        sites_to_check = inv_result.mutation_sites[:max_checks_per_variable]\n\n        for idx, site in enumerate(sites_to_check):\n            # Extract milestone from deliverable_id (e.g. \"D2.3\" -> \"2\")\n            milestone = _extract_milestone(site.deliverable_id)\n            seq = idx + 1\n\n            deliverable_id = f\"D{milestone}.{seq}.inv\"\n\n            # Build description with predicate, mutation reference, and edge cases\n            edge_cases_str = \", \".join(DEFAULT_EDGE_CASES[:3])\n            description = (\n                f\"Invariant check: verify '{entry.invariant_predicate}' \"\n                f\"holds after {site.expression} in {site.deliverable_id}. \"\n                f\"Edge cases: {edge_cases_str}. \"\n                f\"State assertion: assert {entry.invariant_predicate}\"\n            )\n\n            d = Deliverable(\n                id=deliverable_id,\n                description=description,\n                kind=DeliverableKind.INVARIANT_CHECK,\n                metadata={\n                    \"variable_name\": entry.variable_name,\n                    \"scope\": entry.scope,\n                    \"invariant_predicate\": entry.invariant_predicate,\n                    \"mutation_deliverable_id\": site.deliverable_id,\n                    \"mutation_expression\": site.expression,\n                    \"edge_cases\": DEFAULT_EDGE_CASES[:3],\n                },\n            )\n            generated.append(d)\n\n        # Update InvariantEntry with generated verification IDs\n        entry.verification_deliverable_ids = [d.id for d in generated if\n            d.metadata.get(\"variable_name\") == entry.variable_name]\n\n    return generated\n\n\ndef _extract_milestone(deliverable_id: str) -> str:\n    \"\"\"Extract milestone number from deliverable ID.\n\n    Examples:\n        \"D2.3\"   -> \"2\"\n        \"D-0015\" -> \"0015\"\n        \"D4.2\"   -> \"4\"\n    \"\"\"\n    # Try D{number}.{seq} format first\n    m = re.match(r\"D(\\d+)\\.\", deliverable_id)\n    if m:\n        return m.group(1)\n\n    # Try D-{number} format\n    m = re.match(r\"D-(\\d+)\", deliverable_id)\n    if m:\n        return m.group(1)\n\n    # Fallback: use the ID as-is\n    return deliverable_id.lstrip(\"D-\")\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}

   deliverables: list[Deliverable],\n    max_checks_per_variable: int = 5,\n) -> InvariantRegistryOutput:\n    \"\"\"Execute the invariant registry pipeline pass.\n\n    Pipeline:\n    1. Filter to Implement deliverables\n    2. Detect state variables from descriptions\n    3. Generate mutation inventory across all deliverables\n    4. Build InvariantEntry objects with constrained predicates\n    5. Emit verification deliverables\n    6. Check for duplicate variables\n    7. Render registry section markdown\n\n    Idempotent: does not modify input deliverables. Already-generated\n    invariant_check deliverables are filtered out before processing.\n    \"\"\"\n    # Idempotency: filter out previously generated invariant_check deliverables\n    source_deliverables = [\n        d for d in deliverables\n        if d.kind != DeliverableKind.INVARIANT_CHECK\n    ]\n\n    # Variable table\n    lines.append(\"| Variable | Scope | Predicate | Mutation Sites | Verification IDs |\")\n    lines.append(\"|----------|-------|-----------|----------------|------------------|\")\n    for entry in entries:\n        sites_str = \", \".join(ms.deliverable_id for ms in entry.mutation_sites)\n        verif_str = \", \".join(entry.verification_deliverable_ids) or \"none\"\n        lines.append(\n            f\"| `{entry.variable_name}` | {entry.scope} | \"\n            f\"`{entry.invariant_predicate}` | {sites_str} | {verif_str} |\"\n        )\n\n    lines.append(\"\")\n    return \"\\n\".join(lines)\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
